5. ස්වකීය අධීක්ෂණ වගකීම් යථා පරිදි සපුරා තිබීම සහතික කර ගනු පිණිස එෙලසින් වග කිව යුතු නිලධාරින් විසින් නිසි කම සහ කාර්ය පටිපාටීන් අනුගමනය කරනු ලැබ තිෙබ් ද යන වග; 6. ෙමම පරීක්ෂණෙයහි නිගමනයන් පාදක ෙකොට ගනිමින් ඉදිරිෙය් දී විය හැකි එබඳු සිද්ධීන් වළක්වා ලනු පිණිස ගත යුතු කියාමාර්ග නිර්ෙද්ශ කිරීම. රජෙය් ගිණුම් පිළිබඳ කාරක සභාව විසින් අවධාරණය ෙකෙරන පරිදි ආයතන සංගහෙය් විධිවිධාන අනුව පැවැත් විය යුතු අභɕන්තර පරීක්ෂණෙය් විෂයය ක්ෙෂේතය ඉහත සඳහන් ජනාධිපති ෙකොමිෂන් සභාව ෙවත පැවැරුණු 4 වන විෂයය යටතට ඇතුළත් වනවා. එබැවින්, එබඳු අභɕන්තර පරීක්ෂණයක් ඇරඹීම අවශɕ ෙනොවන බව ද පැහැදිලියි. ජනාධිපති ෙකොමිෂන් සභාවක් පත් කිරීම සඳහා වූ අංක 1516/18 හා 2007.09.25 දින දරන අතිවිෙශේෂ ගැසට් නිෙව්දනය හැන්සාඩ් වාර්තාවට ඇතුළත් කිරීම සඳහා ඇමුණුම 19 වශෙයන් මා සභාගත* කරනවා.

ෙමම තත්ත්වය රජෙය් ගිණුම් පිළිබඳ කාරක සභාව ෙවත වාර්තා කිරීෙමන් පසුව වුව ද, 2007.10.19 දින පැවැති එම කාරක සභා රැස්වීෙම් දී ආයතන සංගහෙය් විධිවිධාන අනුව පරීක්ෂණයක් පැවැත්වීෙම් අවශɕතාව නැවත අවධාරණය කළ බැවින්, මුදල් හා කමසම්පාදන අමාතɕාංශෙය් ෙල්කම්වරයා විසින් 2007.10.23 දිනැති ලිපිෙයන් ෙම් පිළිබඳව නැවතත් නීතිපතිවරයාෙගන් උපෙදස් විමසනු ලැබුවා. ඊට අදාළ ලිපියත් හැන්සාඩ් වාර්තාවට ඇතුළත් කිරීම සඳහා ඇමුණුම 20 වශෙයන් මා සභාගත* කරනවා.

ෙම් පිළිබඳව නැවත විමර්ශනය කළ නීතිපතිවරයාෙග් උපෙද්ශය වී ඇත්ෙත්, සිදු වී යැයි කියන VAT වංචාෙව් සියලුම අංශ පිළිබඳව පරීක්ෂා කිරීම ජනාධිපති ෙකොමිසෙම් විෂයය පථයට ඇතුළත් කර ඇති බැවින් එම කරුණු ගැන විමසීම සඳහා අභɕන්තර පරීක්ෂණයක් පැවැත්වීම අවශɕ ෙනොවන බවයි. එබඳු පරීක්ෂණයක් මඟින් එම ෙකොමිසෙම් කටයුතු ද්වීකරණය වීමක් ෙමන්ම එම පරීක්ෂණ ෙකෙරහි කිසි යම් බලපෑමක් සිදු වීමට ඉඩ ඇති බවට ද නිරීක්ෂණය කර තිබුණා. නීතිපතිතුමාෙග් 2007.10.24 දිනැති පිළිතුරු ලිපිය හැන්සාඩ් වාර්තාවට ඇතුළත් කිරීම සඳහා ඇමුණුම 21 වශෙයන් මා සභාගත* කරනවා. දැන් පරීක්ෂණ පැවැත් ෙවමින් තිෙබන ජනාධිපති ෙකොමිෂන් සභාෙව් විෂයය ක්ෙෂේතෙය් 4 වන හා 5 වන විෂයයන් ගැන අවධානය ෙයොමු කරන විට ආයතන සංගහෙය් අවශɕතාවන් ඉටු කිරීම සඳහා පමණක් දැනට සිටින ෙහෝ විශාම ලබා සිටින නිලධාරින් පත් කිරීම තුළින් ෙමම වංචාවට අදාළ ෙතොරතුරු ෙහළිදරවු කර ගැනීමට උත්සාහ ගැනීම ෙයෝගɕ ෙනොවන බව පැහැදිලිය. එබැවින්, නීතිපතිවරයාෙග් නිර්ෙද්ශය පිළිබඳව විෙශේෂ පැහැදිලි කිරීමක් අවශɕ ෙනොෙව් යැයි සිතමි. ෙමම ගරු සභාෙව් ඉස්මතු කළ තවත් කරුණක් වූෙය්, මෑතදී විශාම ගිය ෙද්ශීය ආදායම් ෙකොමසාරිස් ජනරාල්වරයා පරීක්ෂණ අවසන් වනතුරු ඔහුෙග් රාජකාරිවලින් ඉවත් කළ යුතු බවට රජෙය් ගිණුම් පිළිබඳ කාරක සභාව විසින් කර ඇති නිර්ෙද්ශය කියාත්මක ෙනොකිරීම ගැනයි. ෙදපාර්තෙම්න්තු පධානීන් පත් කිරීම, මාරු කිරීම හා විනයානුකූල කටයුතු කිරීම පිළිබඳ බලතල ආණ්ඩුකම වɕවස්ථාව අනුව පැවැරී ඇත්ෙත් අමාතɕ මණ්ඩලයට බැවින්, එබඳු මාරු කිරීමක් කළ හැකිව තිබුෙණ් අමාතɕ මණ්ඩලයට පමණයි. එබැවින් එහි වගකීම මුදල් අමාතɕාංශෙය් ෙල්කම්වරයාට පැවැරීම සාධාරණ ෙනොෙව්. එබඳු ස්ථාන මාරුවීමක් සඳහා මුදල් විෂයය භාර ගරු අමාතɕතුමා හට අමාතɕ මණ්ඩලය ෙවත නිර්ෙද්ශ කළ හැකිව තිබුෙණ් අදාළ නිලධාරියාට විරුද්ධව පැහැදිලිවම එල්ල කළ හැකි ෙචෝදනා ඇති බවට සාක්ෂි ඉදිරිපත් වී තිබුෙණ් නම් පමණි. ෙද්ශීය ආදායම් ෙකොමසාරිස් ජනරාල්වරයා එම තනතුෙර් සිටීෙමන් බාධාවක් විය හැකිව තිබුෙණ්, ආයතන සංගහෙය් විධිවිධාන අනුව පත් කරනු ලැබූ නිලධාරියකු විසින් ෙදපාර්තෙම්න්තුෙව් නිලධාරින්ෙගන් පශ්න කිරීම මඟින් පරීක්ෂණයක් සිදු කරන්ෙන් නම් පමණි. එෙසේ වුවද, අපරාධ අංශෙය් අදාළ පරීක්ෂණ අපරාධ විමර්ශන ෙදපාර්තෙම්න්තුව විසින් ඉටු කර ඇති බැවිනුත්, ෙමම වංචාවට අදාළ අනික් කරුණු ජනාධිපති ෙකොමිසම විසින් පරීක්ෂා කරනු ලබන බැවිනුත් ෙද්ශීය ආදායම් ෙකොමසාරිස් ජනරාල්වරයාට එකී පරීක්ෂණ සම්බන්ධෙයන් කිසිදු බලපෑමක් කිරීමට හැකියාවක් තිබුෙණ් නැහැ. දැනට මහාධිකරණෙය් විභාග ෙවමින් පවත්නා නඩුවට පාදක වූ අධිෙචෝදනා පතය අනුව පැහැදිලි වන්ෙන් අපරාධ පරීක්ෂණ ෙදපාර්තෙම්න්තුෙව් පරීක්ෂණවලින් ෙහළිදරවු වූ පරිදි ෙමම වංචාවට අදාළ නිලධාරින් වශෙයන් හඳුනා ෙගන ඇති නිලධාරින්

[ගරු රංජිත් සියඹලාපිටිය මහතා]

** කථාව අවසානෙය් පළ කර ඇත. உைரயினிᾠதியில் தரப்பட்ᾌள்ளᾐ. Produced at end of speech.

** කථාව අවසානෙය් පළ කර ඇත. உைரயினிᾠதியில் தரப்பட்ᾌள்ளᾐ. Produced at end of speech.

2008 මාර්තු 18 2859 2860

ෙදෙදනා හැර ෙවනත් නිලධාරින් හට ෙචෝදනා ෙගොනු වී ෙනොමැති බවයි. එවකට VAT අංශෙය් ෙසේවය කිරීෙම් ෙහේතුෙවන් ෙමම වංචාවට සම්බන්ධ යැයි ෙචෝදනා එල්ල වන නිලධාරින් ෙමම නීති කෘතɕෙය් දී පැමිණිල්ෙල් සාක්ෂිකරුවන් වශෙයන් නම් සඳහන්ව තිෙබනවා. VAT වංචාවට අදාළ පරීක්ෂණ ජනාධිපති ෙකොමිසම විසින් කර ෙගන යන අතරතුර දී හා මීට අදාළ නඩුව ෙකොළඹ මහාධිකරණෙය් පවත්වා ෙගන යන අවස්ථාවක දී එකී පරීක්ෂණවල නිගමන ලැබීමට ෙපර කිසියම් නිලධාරියකු සම්බන්ධෙයන් පූර්ව නිගමනයට එළඹීම සාධාරණ යුක්තියට පටහැනි කියාවක් විය හැකිව තිබුණා. රජෙය් ගිණුම් පිළිබඳ කාරක සභාෙව් ගරු සභාපතිතුමා විසින් ඉදිරිපත් කරන ලද සාරාංශ වාර්තාෙව් නිර්ෙද්ශ කර ඇති පරිදි එවකට සිටි ෙකොමසාරිස් ජනරාල්වරයා පරීක්ෂණ අවසන් වනතුරු ඔහුෙග් රාජකාරිවලින් ඉවත් කිරීමට කටයුතු ෙනොකිරීම සම්බන්ධෙයන් කරුණු පැහැදිලි කරමින් මුදල් හා කමසම්පාදන අමාතɕාංශෙය් ෙල්කම්වරයා විසින් පාර්ලිෙම්න්තු මහ ෙල්කම්තුමිය ඇමතූ 2008.03.03 දිනැති ලිපිය ද හැන්සාඩ් වාර්තාවට ඇතුළත් කිරීම සඳහා ඇමුණුම 22 වශෙයන් මා සභාගත* කරනවා. • වɕාජ ෙලස VAT ආපසු ෙගවීම සිදු වන බව දැන ගත් අවස්ථාෙව් සිටම VAT ආපසු ෙගවීෙම් කියාවලිය විධිමත් කිරීම සඳහාත්, බදු අංශය ශක්තිමත් කිරීම සඳහාත් පහත සඳහන් පියවරයන් රාශියක් මුදල් අමාතɕාංශය විසින් ෙම් වන විටත් කියාත්මක කරනු ලැබ තිෙබනවා. මුදල් අමාතɕාංශෙය් ෙල්කම්වරයා විසින් එකී පියවර පිළිබඳ සවිස්තර වාර්තාවක් 2007.05.08 දින රජෙය් ගිණුම් පිළිබඳ කාරක සභාෙව් ෙල්කම්වරයා ෙවත ඉදිරිපත් කරනු ලැබ තිෙබනවා. මා එය ඇමුණුම 23 ෙලස හැන්සාඩ් වාර්තාවට ඇතුළත් කිරීම සඳහා සභාගත* කරනවා. එෙසේ ගනු ලැබූ පියවර කිහිපයක් පමණක් සඳහන් කරන්න කැමැතියි. 1. VAT බදු ආපසු ෙගවීම කිරීමට ෙපර බදු විගණනයක් කිරීම අනිවාර්යය කිරීම. 2. අපනයනකරුවන්ට ආපසු ෙගවීෙම් දී ෙර්ගු ෙදපාර්තෙම්න්තුෙව් පරිගණක දත්ත සහ තුලනය කිරීෙමන් පසුව ආපසු ෙගවීම් සිදු කිරීෙම් කියාවලිය තහවුරු කර ගැනීම අනිවාර්ය කිරීම. 3. VAT බදු ආපසු ලබා ගැනීෙම් දී බැංකු ඇපකර (Bank guarantee) ඉදිරිපත් කිරීෙම් අවශɕතාව දැක්ෙවන කමයක් හඳුන්වා දීම. 4. අපනයනකරුවන් සම්බන්ධෙයන් ඔවුන්ෙග් ආනයනවල දී අය කරන VAT අය කිරීම නීතɕනුකූලව කල් දැමීම ෙහවත් බදු විලම්භනය කිරීම තුළින් ආපසු ෙගවීම අවම කර තිබීම. 5. VAT බදු ආපසු ෙගවීමට ෙබෙහවින් අදාළ වන ක්ෙෂේත ෙබොෙහොමයක් VAT බද්ෙදන් නිදහස් කිරීම තුළින් බදු ආපසු ෙගවීෙම් අවශɕතාව නැති කිරීම 6. අපනයනෙය් දී හැර අනිකුත් අවස්ථාවල දී ෙයදවුම් බද්ද, නිමැවුම් බද්ෙදන් සියයට 85කට සීමා කිරීම තුළින් VAT බදු ආපසු ෙගවීම පාලනය කිරීම.

ෙද්ශීය ආදායම් ෙදපාර්තෙම්න්තුෙව් නිලධාරින් අතෙළොස්සක් විසින් සිදු කරන ලද VAT බදු වංචාව පිළිබඳ නිතර නිතර සඳහන් කිරීම තුළින් බදු පරිපාලනය ඉතා පහත් මට්ටමකට වැටී ඇතැයි යන අදහස ජනතාව තුළ ජනිත වනවා. බදු ආදායම ඉහළ නැංවීෙම් කියාවලියට එමඟින් අහිතකර බලපෑමක් සිදු වන බව ෙපන්වා දිය යුතුව තිෙබනවා. ජනතාවෙග් පරිෙභෝජනය මත අය කරන වක බදු ෙවනුවට ඍජු බදු පමාණය වැඩි කිරීමට රජෙය් අවධානය ෙයොමු වී තිෙබනවා. වක බදු නිසා සාමානɕ මහ ජනතාව ෙවත පැටෙවන බදු බර සම්බන්ධෙයන් බලන කල්හි වක බදු ෙවනුවට ඍජු බදු වැඩි කිරීෙම් වැඩ පිළිෙවළක් අවශɕ වී තිෙබනවා. එම කාර්යභාරය පැවැරී ඇත්ෙත් ෙද්ශීය ආදායම් ෙදපාර්තෙම්න්තුවටයි.

ෙමහිදී අප විසින් අමතක ෙනොකළ යුතු කරුණක් නම්, 2004 දී ෙපොදුජන එක්සත් ෙපරමුණ ආණ්ඩුව බලයට පත් වන විට ෙද්ශීය ආදායම් ෙදපාර්තෙම්න්තුව පරිහානිෙය් අගාධයට වැටී තිබූ බවයි. 2002 අංක 10 දරන බදු සමා පනත මඟින් බදු නිලධාරින් ෙබලහීන කර තිබුණා. ආදායම් අධිකාරියක් ඇති කිරීම සඳහා පිඹුරු පත් සකස් ෙවමින් තිබුණා. ෙපොදුජන එක්සත් ෙපරමුණ රජය බලයට පත් වන විට ෙද්ශීය ආදායම් ෙදපාර්තෙම්න්තුෙව් නිලධාරින් අතර දැඩි අසහනයක් තිබුණු අතර, ඔවුන් වෘත්තීය කියාමාර්ගවලට අවතීර්ණ වී සිටියා. කළු ෙකොඩි වɕාපාර සුලභ දර්ශනයක්ව තිබුණා. ෙම් පශ්න හඳුනා ගත් රජය ෙද්ශීය ආදායම් ෙදපාර්තෙම්න්තුව ශක්තිමත් කිරීම සඳහා විෙශේෂ වැඩ පිළිෙවළක් ආරම්භ කළා. බදු සමා පනත අෙහෝසි කර බදු පරිපාලනය ශක්තිමත් කළා. ආදායම් අධිකාරි සංකල්පය ඉවත ලා බදු පනත්වල විධිවිධාන නිසි පරිදි කියා කළ හැකි අන්දමින් ෙදපාර්තෙම්න්තු වɗහය ශක්තිමත් කළා. අවුරුදු 10ක් පුරා කාර්ය මණ්ඩලය බඳවා ෙනොගැනීම නිසා තිබුණ උග ෙසේවක හිඟයට පිළියම් වශෙයන් උපාධිධාරින් දහසකට ආසන්න පිරිසක් මාණ්ඩලික ෙශේණි සඳහා බඳවා ගත්තා. උසස් වීම් ෙනොලද විශාල සංඛɕාවකට උසස් වීම් ලබා දී කාර්ය මණ්ඩලය දිරිමත් කළා.

අෙප් බදු පරිපාලනය යල් පැන ගිය එකක් බවට නිතර ෙචෝදනා ලැෙබන ෙහයින් එය නවීකරණය කිරීෙම් කියාවලිය මීට සමාන්තරව සිදු වුණා. ෙමහිදී විෙශේෂෙයන් සඳහන් කළ යුතුව ඇත්ෙත්, ෙද්ශීය ආදායම් ෙදපාර්තෙම්න්තුෙව් නිලධාරින් නවසියයකට පමණ වසර ෙදකක කාලයක් තුළ දී කිසි යම් විෙද්ශ පුහුණුවක් ලබා දීමයි. ෙමය රජෙය් ෙවනත් කිසිදු ෙදපාර්තෙම්න්තුවක නිලධාරින් ෙනොලැබූ අනුගහයකි.

ෙම් නිසා දිරිමත් වී කටයුතු කරන ෙදපාර්තෙම්න්තුෙව් කාර්ය මණ්ඩලයට පශංසා කළ යුතුයි. 2004 දී බදු ආදායම් දළ ෙද්ශීය නිෂ්පාදිතෙයන් සියයට 2ක් පමණ වුවද, එය 2007 දී සියයට 3 දක්වා වැඩි වී ඇත. මුදල් අමාතɕාංශය විසින් ෙද්ශීය ආදායම් ෙදපාර්තෙම්න්තුෙව් සියලුම මට්ටම්වල නිලධාරින් සමඟ නිති පතා සාකච්ඡා පැවැත්වීම තුළින් ඔවුන්ෙග් කාර්ය සාධනය ඉහළ නැංවීමට කටයුතු කරනවා. ෙද්ශීය ආදායම් ෙදපාර්තෙම්න්තුව ශක්තිමත් කිරීමට ෙමබඳු වැඩ පිළිෙවළක් අතීතෙය්දී කිසිම දිනක කියාත්මක ෙනොවූ බව ෙමම ගරු සභාෙව් මන්තීතුමන්ලා ෙවත අවසාන වශෙයන් මා දන්වා සිටිනවා. මා ෙමම ගරු සභාෙවන් ඉල්ලා සිටින්ෙන් මාෙග් ෙම් සටහනත්, සභාගත කර ඇති ෙල්ඛනත් පරිශීලනය කර නිවැරදි තත්ත්වය තහවුරු කර ගන්නා ෙලසයි.

ෙද වනුව මා ෙමම ගරු සභාෙවන් ඉල්ලා සිටින්ෙන් ෙමම වැට් වංචාවට අදාළ ෙචෝදනා විමර්ශනය කිරීෙම් කටයුතු කර ෙගන යෑමට ගරු අධිකරණයටත්, අෙනකුත් පරීක්ෂණ කටයුතු කර ෙගන යෑමට ජනාධිපති පරීක්ෂණ ෙකොමිෂන් සභාවටත් ඉඩ දී බදු පරිපාලනය ශක්තිමත් කිරීම සඳහා මුදල් අමාතɕාංශය ෙගන යන වැඩ පිළිෙවළට සහෙයෝගය ෙදන ෙලසයි. ගරු මන්තීතුමන්ලාෙගන් මා තවදුරටත් ඉල්ලා සිටින්ෙන්, ෙමම වැට් වංචාවට අදාළ වැදගත් සාක්ෂි තමන් ෙවත ඇත්නම් ජනාධිපති ෙකොමිෂන් සභාව ෙවත ඉදිරිපත් කරන ෙලසයි.

** කථාව අවසානෙය් පළ කර ඇත. உைரயினிᾠதியில் தரப்பட்ᾌள்ளᾐ. Produced at end of speech.

පාර්ලිෙම්න්තුව 2861 2862

මාෙග් මවිතයට ෙහේතු වන කරුණක් වන්ෙන්, ෙමම වැට් වංචාව සිදු වූෙය් 2002 ෙනොවැම්බර් මස සිට 2004 අෙගෝස්තු මස දක්වා කාලය තුළ බැවින් එම කාලෙය් බලෙය් සිටිෙය් එක්සත් ජාතික පක්ෂය බවත් ඇතැමුන්ට අමතක වීමයි. වැට් වංචාෙව් පධාන චූදිතයා වන දැනට අධිකරණය මඟ හරිමින් සිටින පුද්ගලයා එවකට බලෙය් සිටි පක්ෂෙය් විධායක සභිකයකු වූ බව රහසක් ෙනොෙව්. වැට් වංචාව පිළිබඳව පරීක්ෂණ පැවැත්වීම නිසි පරිදි සිදු ෙනොවූ බවට වර්තමාන රජයටත්, මුදල් අමාතɕාංශෙය් වර්තමාන ෙල්කම්වරයාටත් ෙචෝදනා එල්ල කරන අය ෙමම වංචාව සිදු වූ කාලෙය් සිටි මුදල් අමාතɕාංශෙය් ෙල්කම්වරයා ගැන ෙහෝ ෙද්ශීය ආදායම් ෙකොමසාරිස් ජනරාල්වරුන් ගැන කිසිදු සඳහනක් කර නැහැ. වැට් ආපසු ෙගවීෙම් කියාවලිය ආරක්ෂාකාරී පියවරවල් සහිතව හඳුන්වා ෙනොදීම ගැන අදාළ නිලධාරින්ට කිසිවකුත් ෙදොස් කියන්ෙන් නැහැ.

2004 ෙදසැම්බර් මස සිදු වූ සුනාමි වɕසනයට අදාළව ෙකරුණු සහන සැලසීම්, පුනරුත්ථාපන හා පතිනිර්මාණ කිරීෙම් කියාවලිෙය්දී මුදල් අමාතɕාංශයට විශාල කාර්යභාරයක් ඉටු කිරීමට සිදු වූ පසු බිමක වර්තමාන රජයත්, මුදල් අමාතɕාංශෙය් ෙල්කම්වරයාත් වැට් වංචාව සම්බන්ධෙයන් 2005 සිටම අවශɕ පියවර ෙගන තිබීම සැබැවින්ම පශංසාවට ලක් විය යුත්තක්.

ෙමම වංචාවට අදාළ නිලධාරින් ආරක්ෂා කිරීමට අතිගරු ජනාධිපතිතුමාට ෙහෝ එතුමාෙග් රජයට ෙහෝ මුදල් අමාතɕාංශෙය් ෙල්කම්වරයාට ෙහෝ ෙවනත් කිසිදු බලධාරියකුට අවශɕතාවක් ෙනොමැති බව මම නැවතත් අවධාරණය කරනවා. ඔබතුමාට ස්තුතියි.

මුදල් හා කමසම්පාදන අමාතɕාංශය

நிதி, திட்டமிடல் அைமச்சு MINISTRY OF FINANCE AND PLANNING මහ ෙල්කම් කාර්යාලය, ෙකොළඹ 01 ெசயலகம், ெகாᾨம்ᾗ 01 The Secretariat Colombo 01 කාර්යාලය ෆැක්ස් ෙවබ් අඩවිය w.w.w.treasury Gov.lk Office Fax Website මෙග් අංකය ඔෙබ් අංකය දිනය My No. Your No. Date The Attorney General Secrecy Provisions in the Value Added Tax Act No. 14 of 2002 Investigation of Fraudulent VAT Refunds

You are probably aware of the recent media reports relating to fraudulent VAT refunds; the reports were based on certain parts of the Auditor Generals report No. E. H/C//I.R./Wimasum/2004/30 dated 03th June, 2005 (copy annexed). 02. It would appear that some of the refunds have been made to fictitious parties.

(94) 011-2449823 ெவப்ைசட் அᾤவலகம் ெபக்ஸ்

FP/06/20/09/20 உமᾐ இல. திகதி எனᾐ இல. 22.12.2005

03. It is proposed to investigate the matter further with a view to ascertaining whether in fact there has been any fraud and if so, the person or persons responsible for same, the actual amount involved etc.

04. It has been pointed out that the provisions in Sections in sections 73 of the VAT Act relating to official secrecy might stand in the way of any such inquiry. The provisions in the VTA Act appear to be more stringent than those in the Inland Revenue Act (Section 178 of Act 38 of 2000), in that Section 178 provides for a number of exceptions in subsections (4), (5), (6) etc. but there are no such exceptions in Sections 73 of the VAT Act.

05. I wish to have your opinion as to whether an inquiry/investigation by the Fraud Bureau/a person or a panel appointed by the Minister of Finance or by the Cabinet or by H. E. the President etc, would be violative of Section 73 of Act No. 14 of 2002 or whether there is any alternative course of action available to ascertain the matters referred to in paragraph 3.

06. My observations on the applicability of Section 73, as regards the refunds made to fictitious parties, ate as follows:

The substance of Section 73(1) is that the Commissioner General and the other employees of the Inland Revenue Department …………” shall preserve…… secrecy with regard to all matters relating to the affairs of any person ………” the “person” (defined in Section 83 at page 75 as including “a company or body of persons”) in this context is obviously the “taxpayer” - the one who as registered in the relevant records of the Tax Department as such, who furnishes tax returns corresponds with the Tax Department on various issues etc. in other words the persons has to be “real” (not fictitious)

Where the “Persons” who has (allegedly) furnished returns (with other documents in support of the same) claimed (and received) refunds is not real but fictitious, then any inquiry into or investigation of the returns, refund claims and other correspondence would not constitute in law, a violation of the “secrecy relating to the affairs of any persons”, because no “person” exists in reality.

These observations would not apply where the “persons” (i.c., recipients of the refunds) are actual and real.

07. As the sum alleged to have been fraudulently refunded is around Rs. 3,450 Mr. It is necessary to take quick action identify and round up the culprits.

08. I look forward for your advice in this matter.

Sgd. P. B. Jayasundara Secretary of the Treasury

FRAUDULENT VAT REFUNDS

This refers to your letter dated 26th October 2005, the details as requested are kindly setout below. (i) Query - No. 2(i)

No Audit has been carried out each of the cases stated in the list before the issue of respective refunds. However, audits have been carried out subsequently and assessments have been is-sued. This has been brought to your notice by item No.08 of my letter dated 21st September 2005. - No. 2(ii) A detailed list in respect of issue of refund cheques is attached. Where the name of the Assessor who authorized and approved the refund assessment and name of the Deputy Commissioner who certified the document have been indicated respectively. - No. 2(iii) There are two Officers who should signed refund cheques ini-tially it is signed by the Deputy Commissioner In-charge of VAT Refund Branch. Thereafter it is signed by the Chief Accountant. - No. 2(iv) Names of the Deputy Commissioners and Commissioners served in VAT branch during the respective period are as fol-low. Deputy Commissioners Period Mr. R.K.H.Kaluarachchi - from 2002/08/01 to 2003/06/30 Mr. Z.Jayathilake - from 2003/07/01 to 2004/12/31 Commissioners Mr. S.H.Gunawardane - from 2002/08/01 to 2003/09/30 Mr. A.A. Wijepala - from 2003/10/01 to 2004/12/31 (2) Query - No. 3 a(i) The custom of auditing the first refund before issue of the re-fund was not continued with the change over from GST to VAT because of shortage of staff and necessity of issuing the refund within a period of one month. - No. 3 a(ii) The first refund cases available in the list. But, no an audit has been carried out before the issue of refunds. However, Audits have been carried out subsequently. - No. 3(b) In the cases of exporters, refunds were attributable to both the local purchases and import purchases. 1. The input tax has not been checked with the custom information’s before the issue of refund as the facility was not available in the system during the period. 2. As regards the local purchases, the necessary schedules containing the details of inputs have already been ob-tained.

- No. 3(c) Yes, there are some refund claimants who have registered as non-exporters. According to the provisions of the Act refund had to be issued within a period of 90 days, whether the persons is a exporter or non - exporter. On the basis of findings it is suggested that an independent commission of inquiry be appointed to inquire in to these cases where irregularities have been taken place. Further, a copy of the reply to the audit query by Auditor General under reference No.EF/C/IR/Wimasum/2004/30 is attached herewith for your kind consideration. ඇමුණුම්-12 මුදල් හා කම සම්පාදන අමාතɕාංශය

நிதி, திட்டமில் அைமச்சு MINISTRY OF FINANCE AND PLANNING මහ ෙල්කම්කාර්යාල The Secretariat. ෙකොළඹ 01 Colombo 01

23rd Janurary, 2006 Mr. Lalith Weerathunge Secretary to the President Dear Sir, APPOINTMENT OF A COMMISSION OF INQUIRY TO INQUIRE INTO ALLEGED FRAUDULENT VAT REFUNDS As you may be aware, wide publicity was given to alleged fraudulent VAT refunds at the Department of Inland Revenue, based on findings by the Auditor General in his report No: EH/C/IR/vimasum/2004/30, dated June 2005. The then Commissioner General of Inland Revenue (CGIR) on 23rd June 2005 brought to my notice of an Audit query made by the Auditor General’s Department with regard to alleged malpractices involving VAT refunds, amounting to Rs. 3.6 billion to 20 companies through 235 cheques, during the period 15the November 2002 to 25th the August 2004. I was also informed that this matter is being investigated by the Bribery Commission and that in addition and that the CGIR has ap-pointed a committee headed by Mr. P. P. D. P. Karunasekera, the then Addl. Commissioner General as Chairman of this committee. The then CGIR further informed me that he is bringing this matter to my attention in view of his impending retirement on 9th July 2005. In the meantime , Hon. Minister of Finance and Planning also directed me to appoint a suitable officer from the Ministry of Fiancé and Plan-ning to examine this matter. However, as the VAT Act gives full powers to the Commissioner General of Inland Revenue, there was no room for an independent officer of this Ministry to conduct any inquiry. I was also advised that the Secrecy Provisions of the VAT Act (Section 23) do not permit internal Auditors to have access to tax files. In this at background three alternatives were identified; * Request the CGIR to carryout a further inquiry focusing on identified aspects. * Request the Auditor General to carry out a further audit focus-ing on identified aspects. * To establish a Commission under the Commissions of Inquiry Act No. 17 of 1948 to investigate. As such. I wrote to the Commissioner General of Inland Revenue and the Attorney General Seeking clarifications of what action this Ministry could take in this regard, since this matter would have a serious adverse impact on the credibility of the Inland Revenue Department. I wish to note that this matter was also raised in Parliament during the last Budget debate and the Hon. Deputy Minister of Finance and Planning informed the house that the matter has being referred to the Hon. Attorney General for relevant legal advise. After many reminders and follow up corre-spondence with the CGIR. And the Attorney General's Department, I have finally received a response from the CGIR. However I have still not received any response from the Attorney General’s Department. In this background I do not consider that any further delay in action by this Ministry is in the best interest of the public. Since the Commissioner General of Inland Revenue has now documented in his report various information indicating a series of lapses and he, himself who headed the departmental inquiry had advised to appoint and independent inquiry commission to further go into the matter and since it involves an alleged fraud of billions of rupees and there is serious public concern, conduct-ing a high powered inquiry appears to be the correct option Therefore, I kindly request you to consider advising His Excellency the President to appoint a Commission of Inquiry, to look in to this matter

and report within 3 months from the date of such appointment, the find-ings thereof. Considering the seriousness of the alleged fraud and also to ensure an impartial conclusion, in my view, two judges of the Superior Courts may be appointed to go into this matter. Your faithfully, P. B. Jayasundera Secretary to the Treasury Cc; Auditor General Attorney General Commissioner General-IRD My No. CSA/4/Comm/03. March, 07, 2006 OFFICE OF THE PRESIDENT Dr. P. B. Jayasundera Secretary Ministry of Finance & Planning Appointment of a Commission of Inquiry to inquire into alleged Fraudu-lent Vat Refunds I write with reference to your letter dated January 23, 2006 on the above subject. In view of the information and recommendation given in the letter under reference, it has been considered that the appropriate course of action would be establishment of a Commission of Inquiry to inquire into the alleged frauds. I shall therefore be thankful if you could prepare a draft TOR and send me for further action. Pushpa Wellappili Sgd. Lalith Weeratunga Additional Secretary to the President Secretary to the President 13th March, 2006 Secretary to the President Dear Sir, APPOINTMENT OF A COMMISSION OF INQUIRY TO INQUIRE INTO ALLEGED FRAUDULENT VAT REFUNDS Your letter of 7th March, 2006 on the above subject refers. As per your request, I have attached herewith the draft TOR for necessary action. Yours faithfully, P. B. Jayasundera Secretary to the Treasury Terms of Reference Background Auditor General by his report dated 30.06.2005 (Annex 1) has al-leged of malpractices pertaining to VAT refunds which have been made by the Inland Revenue Department during the period 01.10.2002 to 25.08.2004. In response to a communiqué sent by the Secretary to the Treasury, the Commissioner General of Inland Revenue by his letter dated 16.01.2006 (Annex 2) has admitted that there have been irregulari-ties and that an independent Commission of Inquiry be appointed in this regard. Objective and Scope of Work The Commission of Inquiry is required to make an independent investigation into these allegations and make its findings on such allega-tions, along with its recommendations. The Commission is specifically required to investigate and make its findings on the following :

පාර්ලිෙම්න්තුව 2881 2882

1. Whether such VAT refunds have in fact been made to any one or more of the Companies, whose names are more fully men-tioned in Annex 1 ; 2. If such VAT refunds have in fact been made been made, have they been made in contravention of any applicable Statures and/or Guidelines of the Inland Revenue Department ; 3. Are the Companies whose names are mentioned in Annex 1, legally in existence or were in existence at the relevant time : 4. If any irregularities or undue refunds have been made, identify persons who were responsible for such action. The Commission may avail the assistance of any technically compe-tent persons whom it may require to assist in making its findings and any incidental expenditure will be suitably borne. Delivery of the Findings

The Commission is required to make inquiries and submit its report along with recommendations by 30th April 2006. My No. CSA/4/Comm/03. 6 April, 2006 OFFICE OF THE PRESIDENT Secretary Ministry of Finance & Planning Appointment of a Commission of Inquiry to inquire into alleged Fraudu-lent VAT Refunds I write which reference to the draft TOR sent to me by your letter of 13th March 2006, which was subsequently referred to Attorney - Gen-eral for his opinion and comments, The Attorney - General has informed me that there is no legal objection to a commission being appointed under the Commission of Inquiry Act to investigate and report on the relevant matters. Hence, You may please send me the list of companies, which is referred to as Annex I in the draft TOR (copy annexed)

I would also like to inform you that, in view of the on going court case on this matter, it is proposed to appoint a retired Judge of the Supe-rior Courts to chair the said commission. පාර්ලිෙම්න්තුව 2893 2894

ඇමුණුම –17 23rd August 2007 CONFIDENTIAL Hon. Attorney General Attorney General’s Department Colombo 12. Dear Sir, Alleged VAT Fraud - Department of Inland Revenue Further to the telephone conversation I had with you after my having appearing before the Committee on Public Accounts (COPA) which was held on 22.08.2007.

As you are aware, I have been constantly in touch with you and your predecessor with regard to the investigations relating to the aforesaid alleged VAT fraud which was referred to the Criminal Investigations Department (CID) in mid 2006 by this Ministry, on the instructions of His Excellency the President.

This Ministry also commenced related Administrative investigations on the instructions of the then Minister of Finance in early 2005. The then Commissioner General of Inland Revenue (CGIR) having carried out initial investigations over a period of three months submitted his report to me in September 2005, observing that the issue of refunds is a collec-tive activity of a number of officers and as such it is not possible to identify and single-out any individual as being responsible. In one of his reports, the CGIR has named the Deputy commissioners who certified related refund documents but not identified any specific default on the part of any officer.

In view of the complexities involved with this matter associating several parties, including third parties, I was compelled to seek the advise of the Attorney General as to how the investigation should be proceeded with i.e. through a Presidential Commission of Inquiry or in any other authori-tative form through whom third parties could also be summoned. Fur-ther such advise was considered necessary in the light of the specific charges that were being formulated by the CID inter alia through the examination of relevant officials of the Inland Revenue Department.

In the meantime, as I explained to you over the phone at the COPA meetings before which I appeared on 21st-22nd August 2007 pertaining to the Inland Revenue Department, a view was expressed that an admin-istrative inquiry should have been proceeded with in terms of the provi-sions of the Establishments Code. Since this is contrary to the under-standing we had in relation to the manner in which this inquiry should be proceeded with having recognized the associated complexities and the seriousness of the allegations. I seek your views as to whether it is advis-able to appoint an inquiring Officer to conduct an inquiry under the Establishments Code.

If the CID inquiry has now been completed, it may be possible to iden-tify officials against whom specific charges could he framed to proceed with an administrative investigation, in addition to the legal proceedings being handled by the Attorney General’s Department. In this case I would appreciate if you could forward the names of the officials and the

possible charges based on which this Ministry could initiate such admin-istrative investigation. I shall be thankful if you could advise me accordingly.

Yours faithfully

P. B. Jayasundera Secretary to the Treasury

Cc : Secretary to the President.

My Ref. : CRI/109/2006 24th August, 2007 Dr. P. B. Jayasundera, Secretary to the Treasury, Ministry of Finance and Planning, The Secretariat, Colombo 1. ALLEGED VAT FRAUD-DEPARTMENT OF INLAND REVENUE I refer to your letter dated 23rd August 2007. I wish to inform you that it had been decided to forward an indictment against, the following officers namely, Agampodi Gnanasiri de Soysa Jayatilleke and Ananda Wickramasinghe Ambepitiya along with 12 others on charges of con-spiracy to commit misappropriation and misappropriation of state prop-erty to the value of Rs. 399,600,815.55. In view of the magnitude of this fraud and the serious shortcomings in the procedure pertaining to the refund of VAT in the Department of Inland Revenue and to prevent a recurrence of similar offences in the future, I would suggest that you recommend to His Excellency the Presi-dent to appoint a Commission of Inquiry in terms of the Commissions of Inquiry Act No. 17 of 1948 to investigate the commission of the said fraud and irregularities. This would enable the relevant authorities to ascertain the persons directly and indirectly responsible and also to identify the shortcomings in the procedure that existed in the Department of Inland Revenue which would enable the said authorities to make recommendations regarding measures that should be taken to prevent the recurrence of Irregularities and frauds of similar nature in future.

I also wish to inform you that although the CID has conducted very exhaustive investigations in respect of criminal aspects of this fraud there appear to be several other aspects relating to this fraud and other similar acts that may be necessary to be inquired and investigated. Therefore, I believe that this is a matter that should be left to a Commis-sion of Inquiry to investigate and report as suggested above.

Further it is suggested that upon the conclusion of the said inquiry, ap-propriate disciplinary action may be instituted against errant officers as provided for under the Establishments Code. C. R. De Silva, President’s Counsel Attorney General

පාර්ලිෙම්න්තුව 2905 2906

Since certain statements contained in the above document imply that there have been lapses on the part of the Treasury in taking timely ac-tion, I wish to clarify related steps in a chronological order, while also stating reasons for certain actions alleged in the report as having not been taken by the Treasury, I wish to reiterate that actions specified below were taken promptly, despite the intense involvement by the relevant officials, including myself in relief, rehabilitation and recon-struction activities pursuant to the 2004 Tsunami devastation, in relation to which this Ministry had to play a vital role. As already reported to the Committee on Public Accounts by the Treasury officials from time to time, the Inland Revenue Department has taken steps to inquire into alleged fraudulent VAT refunds even before the audit query dated 03.06.2005 received by that Department. The then Commissioner General of Inland revenue, Mr. R.P. L. Weerasinghe having appraised the Ministry, appointed a Committee headed by Mr. P. P. D. P. Karunasekera, Additional Commissioner General of inland Revenue to inquire into this matter based on information received form the Commission to Investigate Allegations of Bribery and Corruption (Annex 1). Upon the receipt of an audit query dated 06.06.2005, Mr. Weerasinghe wrote to me on 23.06.2005 informing that the report of the committee headed by Mr. Karunasekera had not yet submitted and stated that necessary action should be taken without delay in view of Mr. Weerasinghe’s impending retirement on 09.07.2005 (Annx 2). Having apprised the then Hon. Minister of Finance and planning, Dr. Sarath Amunugama also requested to appoint a suitable officer from the minis-try of Finance and Planning to examine into this matter. Accordingly, on 16.08.2005 (Annex 3) the Director - internal Audit was appointed to inquire into this matter, Considering the views expressed by Mr. R. P. L. Weerasinge (Annex 4), who was by that time serving as the Senior Tax Advisor to the ministry of Finance and Planning on the implications of the secrecy provisions on such inquiry, on 12.09.2005 I wrote to the Commissioner General of Inland Revenue to conduct a comprehensive fact - finding inquiry into this matter (Annex 5). In the then Commis-sioner General’s reply dated 21.09.2005, while clarifying certain issues raised has observed that as the as the issue of refund is the collective responsibility of a number of officers, it is not possible to identify and name officers individually responsible for the issue of improper refunds (Annex 6). In the background of totally insufficient clarifications pro-vided, I wrote to the CGIR on 26.10.2005 referring to the relevant part of the Audit query dated 03.06.2005 and instructing to provide informa-tion on specific issues spelt out in my latter. (Annex 7) At this stage a letter was also written to the hon. Attorney General on 21. 10.2005 on the possible implications of the Secrecy provisions in the VAT Act on this inquiry (Annex 8). After repeated reminders the final report was submitted on 16.01.2006 by Mr Karunasekera, who was by then was the Commissioner General, indicating names of several companies involved with the alleged VAT fraud and suggesting that an Independent Com-mission of Inquiry be appointed to inquire into this case (Annex9). In this background, having discussed with the Attorney General a letter was written by me to the Secretary to the President (with copies to both At-torney General and the Auditor General) on 23.01.2006 that a Presiden-tial Commission of inquiry be appointed to look into this matter (Annex 10). Having apprased His Excellency the president of this situation, the matter was referred to the Criminal investigations Department (CID) in mid 2006 which led to the Attorney General having indicted 2 officers of the Inland Revenue Department and 12 other in the High Court of Co-lombo. In consultation with the Hon. Attorney General, an inquiry under the Establishments Code was not held in view of several factors such as the complexities associated with the alleged fraud. The likely adverse impli-cations of such inquiry on the ongoing CID investigation. The implica-tions of Secrecy Provisions in the VAT Act and the impending appoint-ment of a Presidential Commission of Inquiry which has much wider powers than an inquiring officer appointed under the Establishments Code. However, on 22.08.2007 having appreciated the views expressed by the Committee on Public Accounts (COPA) that a domestic inquiry should be conducted in terms of the provisions contained in the Estab-lishments Code, the Hon. Attorney General’s specific advice was sought on the matter in August 2007 (Letter of Secretary to the Treasury to the Hon. Attorney General dated 23.08.2007 - Annex 11). The advice was that in view of the magnitude of the fraud and the seriousness of the shortcomings in the procedure relating to the connected VAT refunds in the Inland Revenue Department, to have a Presidential Commission of

Inquiry to probe into the matter inter alia to identify persons directly and indirectly responsible, the procedural shortcomings and preventive ac-tion that could be taken to prevent the recurrence of irregularities of a similar nature in the future and that on the conclusion of such inquiry appropriate disciplinary action may be instituted against errant officers (Attorney General’s advise dated 24.08.2007 - Annex 12). Accordingly the Treasury requested the Secretary to the President to expedite the appointment of a Presidential Commission of Inquiry in this regard and also provided a revised draft Terms of Reference that was cleared by the Hon. Attorney General. (Letter of Secretary to the Treas-ury to the Secretary to the President - Annex 13, copy of the Gazette Notification appointing the Presidential Commission of Inquiry includ-ing the Terms of Reference - Annex 14 and related Attorney General’s clearance - Annex 15). A State Counsel has been nominated by the Attorney General as provided for in the relevant statute, to assist the Commission and the proceedings are in progress. In the meantime, the criminal case is now being heard by the High Court of Colombo on a continuous basis to ensure early conclusion. However, in the light of further insistence of the members of COPA on 19.10.2007, to conduct a domestic inquiry, advice of the Attorney General was sought again in October 2007. (Letter of Secretary to the Treasury to the Hon. Attorney General dated 23.10.2007 - Annex 16). The Hon. Attorney General opinioned that the mandate of the Presiden-tial Commission of Inquiry that has been appointed covers all aspects of the alleged fraud and it is not necessary to hold a domestic inquiry as it would amount to duplication of the proceedings and also may affect the inquiry by the Commission. (reply of the hon. Attorney General dated 26.10.2007 - Annex 17). Specific actions taken by the Treasury pertaining to the fraudulent VAT refunds and the administrative as well as legal measures that have been taken to strengthen the tax administration to prevent the occurrence of similar frauds in the future , have been explained to COPA in “Report No. 1 - Value Added Tax (VAT) fraud and related issues’ which was forwarded by me on 08.05.2007 (Annex 18). This shows that the Treas-ury has taken action with the identification of relevant issues. I may mention that the reports of the Auditor General on the annual accounts of the Inland Revenue Department for the years 2002 and 2003 had not identified any fraudulent activity connected to this matter despite the fact that there is a unit of the Auditor General’s Department which is opera-tional in-house, at the Inland Revenue Department. As the appointment, transfer, dismissal and disciplinary control of heads of Departments are matters which cannot be delegated by the Cabinet of Ministers in term of the Constitution, you will no doubt agree that this is a matter for the Cabinet of Ministers. I may also mention that all information and clarifications were made available by the Govern-ment members at the Parliamentary debate specifically held on this issue. In addition, the Honourable Minister of State Revenue and Fi-nance also updated Parliament in this regard, form time. Further, His Excellency the president who is also the minister of Finance is being regularly appraised in this regard and His Excellency has instructed the Treasury to proceed as per the advice of the Honouable Attorney Gen-eral. In the circumstance, I wish to inform that as advised by the Hon. Attorney General, appropriate action will be taken based on findings and recommendations of the Presidential Commission of inquiry. I apologize for the delay in responding to this letter. Yours faithfully P. B. Jayasundara Secretary to the Treasury REPORT I Value added Tax (VAT) fraud and related issues Introduction The note is organized as fallows; (a) Operational features of Vat (b) A brief on the VAT fraud. (d) Specific action taken so far(d) Measures taken since 2004 to control the VAT refund system and strengthen revenue 1. Operational Features of VAT 1.1 VAT VAT was introduced from 01.08.2002, in terms of Value Added Tax Act No.14 of 2002, in place of Good and Services Tax (GST) and National Security Levy (NSL) that was in operation. The key features of VAT; * Tax threshold is Rs. 1.8 million per year * Two tax rates of 10 and 20 percent were applicable * All exports were zero rated (all input taxes are refunded * Input tax was allowed to be claimed from output tax * Exempted items are not eligible for refunds 1.2 The Initial Operational Structure VAT was initially operated by under a separate Unit headed by a Commissioners of the Department of Inland Revenue (IRD). Fur-ther, there were four sub branches in the VAT Unit that were Headed by four Deputy Commissioners. The four branches were; * VAT Audit 1 and Registration * VAT Audit 2 * VAT Audit 3 and VAT Refunds * VAT Audit 4 and Collection Please see Annex 1 for a copy of the organization structure. 1.3 The Refund Procedure 1.3.1 Normal Category * When a return of a tax payer claiming a refund is received by the IRD on VAT, after having verified, the return is sent to the Computer Branch to proceed with data entry. * Thereafter the Refund List generated by the C o m p u t e r Branch is submitted to the VAT Audit Branch to proceed with the refund assessment. Having carried out a desk audit or a field audit as may be appropriate; an Assessor authorizes the refund assessment. * Thereafter a Tax Officer in the VAT Audit Branch prepares the refund assessment and another Tax Officer in the same branch verifies the Correctness of the refund assessment.

* The refund is then approved by an Assessor in the VAT Audit Branch on the basis of the Assessment and in subse quently certified by a Deputy Commissioner and sent to the Refunds Branch to make the refund. * One signatory to a refund cheque is a Deputy Commissioner of the Refunds Branch and the other Signatory is the Chief Accountant of the IRD. 1.3.2 Exports * When a return from an exporter claiming a refund a refund is recived by the IRD on VAT, the return is sent to the Com puter Branch to proceed with data entry. * Thereafter the Refund List generated by the Computer Branch is Submitted to the VAT Audit Branch to proceed with the refund assessment. * Then a Tax Officer, in the Vat Audit Refund Branch pre pares the credit voucher in relation to any Import tax de- ferred amount. An Assessor of the VAT Refunds branch verifies the schedule of input tax on local purchases submit- ted by the exporter. * Another Tax Officer in the same branch verifies the correct ness of the input tax refund assessment. * The refund is then approved by an Assessor in the VAT Au- dit/ Refund Branch on the basis of the assessment and subse- quently certified by a Deputy Commissioner and sent to the Refunds Branch to make the refund. However until 2004, such refunds have been made for exporters without verifica- tion of exports. * One signatory to a refund cheque is a Deputy Commissioner of the Refunds Branch and the other signatory is the Chief Accountant of the IRD. 2. A Brief Overview 2.1. At the Treasury Cash Management meetings that were held Ministry of Finance and planning (MoFP) in mid 2004, it was noted that the amount of monthly VAT refunds of around Rs. 2,000 million is excessive, considering the amount of exports, the likely eligible VAT refunds and the large cash outflows. It was also observed that a realistic level of VAT refunds cannot be in excess of Rs. 1, 200 million per month. While taking steps to closely monitor the refunds, certain employees in the IRD started responding by bring to the notice of the (MoFP), that VAT refunds are being made without a sufficient verification and audit process. As such the Commissioner General of Inland Revenue (CGIR) was requested to closely examine the VAT refund process and take appropriate action to arrest the situation. It was then revealed that the were irregularities in the VAT refund Process. 2.2 On the instructions of the minister of finance, a process of any….. this regard. Although initial instructions were for the MoFP to appoint an inquiring officer, the law did not make provision for such intervention. Then the CGIR was requested to provide information pertaining to the alleged irregularities, and a considerable period of time was taken by him to submit a response and the CGIR confirmed to the MoFP that irregularities have taken place. Subse-quently, a large scale tax fraud that had taken place since August 2002 was reported in an Auditor General’s report. The MoFP submitted this information to the Presidential Secretariat requesting the appointment of a Commission of Inquiry. This matter was brought to the notice of His Ex-cellency the President and thereafter the Criminal investi-gations Department (CID) was entrusted to carry-out the necessary investigations in consultation with the Attorney General. As such, the Auditor General's report was also handed over to the CID.

පාර්ලිෙම්න්තුව 2909 2910

2.3 The amount of Rs. 3.5 billion which was reported in the Auditor General Report of 3rd June 2005 as involving the VAT fraud was verified. The CID having conducted exten-sive investigations has informed that they have found suffi-cient evidence to institute legal action and is awaiting advice of the Attorney General who has been apprised of the seriousness of the situation. This matter is handled under the direct supervision of the Inspector General of Police (IGP) as well as the Attorney General. As a initial measure, personal assets some of the suspects have been frozen and several suspects are in the remand prison. 2.4 A summary of fraudulent transactions involving the VAT fraud is given in Annex. II. Out of the 20 reported refund cases, 7 cases are in respect of claims over Rs. 200 million each, which total to a value of Rs. 1,916 million. 5 cases involve Rs 100-500 million each, and further 5 cases in-volve Rs. 150-200 million each. 2.5 The MoFP also examined the possibility of appointing Presidential Commission of inquiry. The advice of the Attorney General's Department was that it is not advisable, since the ongoing CID Investigations would soon lead to a judicial process. The process pursued by the CID and the Attorney General’s Department is also directly followed by His Excellency to President. In the meantime, MoFP has also taken steps to prevent the occurrence of such frauds in the tax administration, in the future. Consequent to several legal and administrative measures that were introduced since 2004, the monthly refunds have been reduced to a level consistent with realistic input credit. 3. Specific Action 3.1 by the CID/Attorney General 3.1.1 A large number of officials of the IRD have been questioned by the CID. 3.1.2. Seven prime suspects have been arrested and pro-duced before courts. They are in Remand prison. 3.1.3. CID is looking for 11 other suspects who have not yet been located. Although there is no official evi-dence, the CID suspects that they may have fled the country. Therefore the CID has requested the sup-port of the Interpol, to arrest these suspects. 3.1.4. CID is awaiting clearance from the Attorney Gen-eral, to proceed with court action. 3.2. By the IRD 3.2.1. The amounts taken by) fraudulent exporters have been treated as Tax liabilities and assessment notices have been issued to all 20 related companies. 3.2.2. Legal actions were instituted in terms of the Value added Tax Act to recover such liabilities. 3.2.3. IRD has not been able to deliver three such assess-ment notices since the related parities are not avail-able at the given addresses. 3.2.4. 5 appeals have been received by the IRD against such assessment notices. 3.2.5. 3 cases have already been called by courts 3.2.6. Passport shave been suspended in appropriate cases. 3.2.7. In terms of the provision of the Value added Tax Act, action is being taken to appropriately freeze the movable and immovable assets of the suspects.

3.2.8. Refund and audit functions of the IRD have been distinctly separated to ensure proper checks and balances. 3.2.9. A dedicated refunds unit has been setup to carry out Export Refunds. 3.2.10.In order to strengthen the tax administration, recruit-ment of new employees was completed and the VAT administration has been strengthened. 3.3. By the Ministry 3.3.1. Regular monitoring of inflows and outflows is en-sured the monthly cash flow meetings. 3.3.2. Administrative and legal changes were introduced to the operational structure of the VAT system. 3.3.3. The investigation on the VAT fraud is being fol-lowed. 3.3.4. Ministry has also sought legal advice to ensure proceeding with the related court cases expedi-tiously. 4. Measures taken in 2004 to strengthen the VAT administration 4.1 Cash release for refunds The Treasury releases funds requested by the IRD for VAT refunds. The monthly gross revenue figures and the refunds made by the IRD are given in Annex III. As would be seen form such date, the amount of refunds has been high throughout 2003 and till August 2004. Thereafter the aver-age level of refunds has reduced and remained below Rs. 1.2 billion per month. Another system weakness observed in the operations of the VAT refund process till 2004 is that both the audit and refund processes have been undertaken by VAT Audit 3 and VAT Refunds Unit. This has compromised the relevant checks and balance in the refund process. In many in-stances, the Assessor who has authorized the refund and the Assessor who approved the refund had been one and the same person. The authorizing officer of this arrange-ment appears to have grossly overlooked the risks associ-ated with such arrangement. 4.2. Changes made after 2004 As shown in Table I and Table II, the VAT revenue and the magnitudes of VAT refunds as a percentage of revenue, particularly in 2003 and the first three quarters of 2004 should have caused concern. Table –I VAT Revenue-2002-2006 2002 2003 2004 2005 2006 Gross Revenue 96,227 115,845 137,544 150,931 175,729 Refunds 9,171 18,650 17,992 12,181 11,174 Net Revenue 86,056 97,195 120,252 138,650 164,555 Refund as a Percentage 9.5 16.l 12.6 8.1 6.4 Of Gross Revenue Source: Department Inland Revenue Department of fiscal Policy Department of Treasury Operations

2008 මාර්තු 18 2911 2912

Table –II VAT Refunds as percentage of VAT Revenue (Quarterly Basis) Year 1st 2nd 3rd 4th Quarter Quarter Quarter Quarter 2002 7.0 9.6 10.2 11.4 2003 13.5 14.9 19.3 16.1 2004 13.9 15.1 14.5 8.7 2005 9.1 7.2 8.8 7.8 2006 8.8 5.9 5.0 6.1 Source: Department fiscal Policy Having examined the procedure that had been in operation in relation to the refund process, it is evident that there had been insufficient checks and balances in place pertaining to VAT refunds. This situation had got aggravated since there had been no verification process between the Inland Revenue and Customs on imports/exports data. The seemingly large sums of money which have been released on account of VAT refunds, appears to have gone unnoticed. Having observed that the volumes of refunds were unrealistic, a two pronged approach was adopted from the latter part of 2004, to arrest this situation. One approach was to strengthen the legal framework inter alia by closing any loopholes associated with the VAT refund process/reducing the scope for refunds. The other was to take administrative measures to streamline the VAT refund process. 4.3 Legal Measures 2004 * Introduction of the VAT deferment system for the apparel industry which is the sector involving the largest volume of VAT refunds due to importation of textiles and other re-lated items. This was implemented through the textile Quota Board on the basis that no VAT is charged on in imported inputs of any apparel exporter, resulting in their being no associated VAT refunds. 2005 * Tea sector was exempted from VAT, resulting in there being no associated VAT refunds. * New rate bands were introduced with resulting restrictions on VAT refunds; 5 percent band-not entitled for VAT refunds. 20 percent band-only up to 15 percent entitled for VAT refunds. 2006 * Vat deferment system was extended to cover domestic purchases of the apparel industry. * A system of expediting VAT refunds on the strength of a Bank Guarantee was introduced paving way for effective verification / audit, while facilitating ‘hurried’ refunds.

2007 * Limiting VAT input tax claim to a maximum of 85 percent of the output tax other than those eligible for zero rated VAT. With this measure, the risk of having undue refunds under the normal category referred to above has been eliminated.

* Electricity and Furness Oil, Diesel, LP Gas being exempted from VAT resulting in there being no associated VAT refunds. * Input claims on motor cars were removed resulting in there being no associated VAT refunds. 4.4 Administrative Measures * A dedicated account was opened with the Central Bank of Sri Lanka in the name of the Commissioner General of Inland Revenue into which 10 percent of all VAT collected by Customs at the point of import is credited, to enable VAT refunds. Any extra funds required had to be obtained from the Treasury upon specific requests. This has helped to streamline the refund process, while also placing more stringent checks and balances. * A Vat refund is made only after setting off any taxes in default. * IRD and Customs were interlinked through an IT system enabling the verification of import / export data and shar-ing of information. This was further extended to cover the Textile Quota Board, Board of Investment and the Export Development Board. The verification of input refunds against actual exports prevents the occurrence of non-existing exporters claiming VAT refunds. * Audit functions of the IRD were strengthened inter alia through the introduction of a compulsory audit pertaining to those who claim over 3 refunds. * Audit and refund functions of the IRD have been distinctly separated to ensure checks and balances. Earlier, both these functions were under the same Deputy Commis-sioner. * In respect of domestic inputs used for zero rated items, a risk based audit system is being introduced.

It may be noted that despite having introduced all such legal and administrative measure, possibilities of malprac-tices cannot be ruled-out, such as through the submission of false VAT invoices for input claims. As such, continu-ous improvements to audit and surveillance measures are a necessity.

4.5 Staffing and Training * IRD was understaffed for many years despites several new and advanced forms of taxes having been introduced. Having established a new organizational structure in 2005/6, recruitment of Assessors, and Tax Officers has now, been completed and promotions to Commissioner, Deputy Commissioner positions were put in place. The cadre positions for senior grades have been expanded and related promotions have also been completed. General training and specific training have also been af-forded to the staff of IRD to provide the necessary knowl-edge and skills. A Code of Ethics and Conduct was introduced to promote staff quality and professional standards.
